## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The governing equation is a second-order nonlinear ODE, with restoring forces that are nonlinear functions of x and possibly nonlinear damping in v.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic spring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Asymmetric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type damping)
- Full Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (mixed damping)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) ŌåÆ symmetric double-well or hardening/softening spring potential
- Terms of the form x**2 * v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type self-excitation
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system (conservative or dissipative without external drive)
- Sign of cubic term: positive c1*x**3 with negative c0*x ŌåÆ double-well potential; negative c1*x**3 ŌåÆ softening spring
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v**3) represent dissipative forces; even powers (v**2) represent direction-dependent drag
- If t appears only inside sin/cos, the system is periodically driven ŌĆö look for resonance phenomena
- Energy-like invariants suggest conservative systems: check if dv_dt can be written as -dU/dx for some potential U(x)
- Products x*v indicate phase-space-dependent forces, breaking time-reversal symmetry

**GT:** `-0.0493727*v┬│ - 1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

Simplifying the GT:
- `0.41553*sin(t)` ŌĆö a sin(t) term
- `-1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x` = `-1.02930*0.02227*t*x - 1.02930*x - 1.02930*x` = `-0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x`
- `-0.04937*v┬│` ŌĆö a v┬│ term
- `-0.29167*|v|^(1/3)` ŌĆö an |v|^(1/3) term

So GT = `0.41553*sin(t) - 2.05860*x - 0.02293*t*x - 0.04937*v┬│ - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

The key components are:
1. `sin(t)` term
2. Linear `x` term
3. `t*x` term
4. `v┬│` term
5. `|v|^(1/3)` term

The `|v|^(1/3)` term is particularly distinctive. Let me check which candidates could potentially represent this.

Looking at candidates with `v**c` type terms that could capture both `v┬│` and `|v|^(1/3)`:

**Candidate 50:** `c0*tanh(c1 + x) + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*v┬▓*x + c6*(c7 + v)**c8`

This has `(c7+v)**c8` which with c7=0 gives `v**c8`, but this only gives one power of v, not both v┬│ and |v|^(1/3). Also, `tanh(c1+x)` can't produce linear x and t*x terms. **No match.**

**Candidate 24:** `c0*x + c1*x┬│ + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*v**c6 + c7*v┬│ + c8*v┬▓*x`

Has `v**c6` (could be |v|^(1/3)? No, `v**c6` isn't `|v|**c6`), `v┬│`, sin term, x term. But no `t*x` term. **No match.**

**Candidate 32:** `c0*x + c1*x┬│ + c2*v + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*v**c7 + c8*v┬▓*x`

No `t*x` term. **No match.**

The GT has `|v|^(1/3)` which requires `Abs(v)`. None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)`. This is a critical issue.

However, if we consider that in practice `|v|^(1/3)` cannot be represented by `v^c` for any c (since `v^(1/3)` is odd while `|v|^(1/3)` is even in v), then no candidate can exactly match.

But wait - could candidates approximate this by combining terms? `|v|^(1/3)` is an even function of v. None of the candidates have `Abs(v)` explicitly.

Let me reconsider: maybe the GT can be approximated but not exactly matched. The question asks for mathematical equivalence for ALL values of v, x, t.

Since `|v|^(1/3)` is even in v and none of the candidates can produce an even fractional power of |v|, no candidate can exactly match the GT.

Actually, let me reconsider candidates with `v**c` terms. If c=1/3, we get `v^(1/3)` which is odd (or undefined for negative v in reals), not `|v|^(1/3)` which is even. These are fundamentally different functions.

No candidate contains `Abs(v)` or any mechanism to produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

Therefore, no candidate can be mathematically equivalent to the GT for all values of the variables.

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-0.0493727*v┬│` ŌĆö cubic in v
- `-1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x` = `-1.02930*0.02227*t*x - 1.02930*x - 1.02930*x` = `-0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x`

- `-0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

So GT = `0.41553*sin(t) - 0.04937*v┬│ - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3) - 2.05860*x - 0.02293*t*x`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `sin(t)` ŌĆö sinusoidal in t
2. `v┬│` ŌĆö cubic in v
3. `|v|^(1/3)` ŌĆö fractional power of |v|
4. `x` ŌĆö linear in x
5. `t*x` ŌĆö product of t and x

No constant offset term, no `tanh`, no `exp`.
